class=\"second-wide-sidebar\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<article id=\"post-424300\" class=\"boxed-class post-424300 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-general even\">\n\t<!-- Search, Blog index, archives, single blog post -->\n\t\t\t<div class=\"boxed-content\">\n\t\t\t<header class=\"clear\">\n  \t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">\n              \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424300/death-penalty-lets-be-honest/\" title=\"Permalink to Death Penalty: Let’s Be Honest\" rel=\"bookmark\">Death Penalty: Let’s Be Honest</a>\n                      </h1>\n          <div class=\"entry-meta table\">\n            <div class=\"table-cell\">\n              \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar member-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/rodin/profile/\" title=\"Rodin has started 132 conversations\">\n\t\t    <img src=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/avatars/21707/58c202a6c5851-bpfull.jpg\" class=\"avatar user-21707-avatar avatar-96 photo\" width=\"96\" height=\"96\" alt=\"Profile photo of Rodin\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role member-avatar-badge\">Member</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a class=\"url fn n\" href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/rodin/profile/\" title=\"Rodin has started 132 conversations\" rel=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\tRodin\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-21T16:00:36+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 21, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline -->\n\t<div class=\"entry-sub-actions\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424300/death-penalty-lets-be-honest/#comments\" title=\"54 Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">54</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p>Jonah Goldberg has an excellent piece today on the <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.nationalreview.com/article/446926/death-penalty-opponents-dishonest-arguments?utm_source=jolt&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=Jolt_4/21/2017&amp;utm_term=Jolt\">dishonesty of the opponents of the death penalty.</a>&nbsp;He highlights two points: (1) opponents create the situation (costs of litigation and associated administration) which they argue should be a basis for discarding the death penalty, and (2) they call it “unconstitutional” when the death penalty is actually written in the constitution (see 5th Amendment). They also point to the numbers of individuals on death row that have been determined to be innocent prior to their delayed executions. That is not an argument against the death penalty unless you really believe we cannot do a better job in investigating and adjudicating the innocence or guilt of people. Is it better to house an innocent person in jail for the rest of their life than to execute them? After all, eliminating the death penalty may actually reduce support for post-conviction innocence proceedings.\n</p><p>One can have a principled argument against the death penalty — but none of the ones put forward are actually that. The real question in my mind is one of relative value: Is the accused’s life of more value than the victim’s? If your answer is “no” you cannot be against the death penalty. You can be for better investigative and prosecutorial rules — eliminate practices that evoke false confessions, make the prosecutors focus on justice instead of political favor — you can be for limiting the penalty to those cases only where a life is taken, and you can be for quick and relatively painless executions, but you cannot be for the eliminating the death penalty altogether.</p> class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p><img class=\"alignright size-medium wp-image-424433\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832-300x207.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"207\" srcset=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832-300x207.jpeg 300w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832-150x104.jpeg 150w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832-600x414.jpeg 600w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832-624x431.jpeg 624w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/shutterstock_115509832.jpeg 637w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\">Saturday is Earth Day — an annual event first launched on April 22, 1970. The inaugural festivities (organized in part by then hippie and now convicted murderer <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2012/apr/20/earth-days-dark-side-789496388/?page=all\">Ira Einhorn</a>) predicted death, destruction and disease unless we did exactly as progressives commanded.\n</p><p>Sound familiar? Behold the coming apocalypse, as predicted on and around <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://reason.com/archives/2000/05/01/earth-day-then-and-now/print\">Earth Day, 1970</a>:</p> <div    \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar contributor-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/jamespethokoukis/profile/\" title=\"James Pethokoukis Pethokoukis\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-21T09:45:37+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 21, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline             <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p><img class=\"alignright size-medium wp-image-424318\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/RTS1368O-e1492712676834-300x200.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" srcset=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/RTS1368O-e1492712676834-300x200.jpg 300w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/RTS1368O-e1492712676834-150x100.jpg 150w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/RTS1368O-e1492712676834.jpg 500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\">Sure, Donald Trump mused about returning to the gold standard during the campaign. But as president, he’s really more of a steel bug than a gold bug. “American steel” to be specific. To Trump, the decline in steel production and steel worker’s jobs are emblematic of lost American greatness. And when Big Steel is back, so will be America. As Trump <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.aei.org/publication/donald-trump-american-steel-another-story-of-economic-nostalgia/\">put it</a> last summer: “We are going to put American-produced steel back into the backbone of our country. This alone will create massive numbers of jobs.”\n</p><p>So with his First 100 Days almost complete, Trump is looking to make a down-payment on his American steel promise. <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-steel-idUSKBN17M237\">Reuters reports</a>:</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a class=\"url fn n\" href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/jamielockett/profile/\" title=\"Jamie Lockett has started 60 conversations\" rel=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\tJamie Lockett\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-21T08:42:55+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 21, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline -->\n\t<div class=\"entry-sub-actions\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424306/the-question-i-would-have-asked/#comments\" title=\"27 Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">27</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p>Last night I had the good fortune to be invited to an event at the Ronald Reagan Presidential Foundation &amp; Institute in Simi Valley, CA entitled “A Nation Engaged: Power and The Presidency” hosted by NPR News and featuring our beloved patron and founder @peterrobinson and noted Reagan historian Craig Shirley. The discussion that flowed from this pairing of Reagan aficionados was not quite what I expected (although given the participants and the venue not entirely surprising) but, as always with these kinds of things, very enlightening.\n</p><p>The evening began with the audience being lead through the Pledge of Allegiance, and as an immigrant I must say that these small slices of American ritual really do provide a sense of community and shared identity. While my libertarian lizard brain rebels at the idea of pledging allegiance to any government or flag, my sense of American-ness was moved.</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424306/the-question-i-would-have-asked/\" class=\"more-link fr button\">More</a>  <div class=\"ricochet-share-toolbar\">\n    <a title=\"Share this Post on Facebook.\"            \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424223/champs-elysees-attack-election/\" title=\"Permalink to The Champs-Elysées Attack and the Election\" rel=\"bookmark\">The Champs-Elysées alt=\"Profile photo of Claire Berlinski, Ed.\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role editor-avatar-badge\">Editor</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">52</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p><img class=\"alignright wp-image-424256 size-medium\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-300x200.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" srcset=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-300x200.jpg 300w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-150x100.jpg 150w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-768x512.jpg 768w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-600x400.jpg 600w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-624x416.jpg 624w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en-750x500.jpg 750w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/2048x1536-fit_des-policiers-a-proximite-des-champs-elysees-le-20-avril-2017-alors-qu-une-fusillade-a-eclate-en.jpg 1400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\">I’m sure you’ve heard that last night, a terrorist opened fire on the police on the Champs-Elysées, killing a police&nbsp;officer and wounding three more. The security forces&nbsp;quickly shot&nbsp;him dead. The Champs-Elysées was evacuated, though it’s back to normal now.&nbsp;It&nbsp;seems there’s still a&nbsp;suspect at large, though news of this is only breaking now and sketchy. (Update: It’s being reported that police have detained three of the terrorist’s family members, but I haven’t seen confirmation of this.)&nbsp;The attacker was as usual known to police; he’d been&nbsp;arrested in February on suspicion of plotting to kill officers but released for&nbsp;of lack of evidence.\n</p><p>Although terrorism always takes you a bit by surprise, I’ve never been less surprised by a terrorist attack in any city I’ve ever lived in. We all knew full well this was highly&nbsp;likely to&nbsp;happen before the election on Sunday. It’s been the subject of much grim speculation here and black humor. An&nbsp;attack was just recently thwarted in Marseilles. I’d be equally unsurprised if there’s another one&nbsp;before Sunday.</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424223/champs-elysees-attack-election/\" class=\"more-link fr class=\"boxed-content\">\n\t\t\t<header class=\"clear\">\n  \t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">\n              \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424121/march-for-science/\" title=\"Permalink to March for Science\" rel=\"bookmark\">March for Science</a>\n                      </h1>\n          <div class=\"entry-meta table\">\n            <div class=\"table-cell\">\n              \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar contributor-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/monacharen/profile/\" title=\"Mona Charen has started 129 conversations\">\n\t\t    <img src=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/avatars/4252/avatar-bpfull-bpthumb.jpg\" class=\"avatar user-4252-avatar avatar-96 photo\" width=\"96\" height=\"96\" alt=\"Profile photo of Mona Charen\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role contributor-avatar-badge\">Contributor</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a class=\"url fn n\" href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/monacharen/profile/\" title=\"Mona Charen has started 129 conversations\" rel=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\tMona Charen\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-20T12:20:20+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 20, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline -->\n\t<div class=\"entry-sub-actions\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424121/march-for-science/#comments\" title=\"19 Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">19</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p><img class=\"alignright size-medium wp-image-424122\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_-300x300.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_-300x300.jpeg 300w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_-150x150.jpeg 150w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_-400x400.jpeg 400w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_-200x200.jpeg 200w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/lHcwDgk_.jpeg 461w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\">Do you have march fatigue yet? The left apparently does not, so we’re in for some street theater on Earth Day, April 22, with the so-called March for Science.\n</p><p>It’s hard to think of a better way to undermine the public’s faith in science than to stage demonstrations in Washington, DC and around the country modeled on the Women’s March in January.</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/424121/march-for-science/\" class=\"more-link fr button\">More</a>  <div class=\"ricochet-share-toolbar\">\n    <a title=\"Share this Post on Facebook.\" format-standard hentry category-group-writing tag-2017-april-group-writing tag-orthodox-jewish-life tag-water even\">\n\t<!-- Search, Blog index, archives, single blog post -->\n\t\t\t<div class=\"boxed-content\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/member-feed/recommended/\" class=\"header-member-promoted\" title=\"Promoted from the Ricochet Member Feed by members\"><img class=\"member-promoted-icon\" width=\"18\" height=\"18\" alt=\"Ricochet Member Recommended Feed\" title=\"Ricochet Member Feed\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/themes/boss-child/images/member-promoted-icon.png\"><span class=\"member-promoted\">Recommended&nbsp;by&nbsp;R&gt;&nbsp;Members</span></a>\t\t\t<header class=\"clear\">\n  \t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">\n              \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/\" title=\"Permalink to Balanit: My Life as a “Mikveh Lady”\" rel=\"bookmark\">Balanit: My Life as a “Mikveh Lady”</a>\n                      </h1>\n          <div class=\"entry-meta table\">\n            <div class=\"table-cell\">\n              \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar member-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/littlemy/profile/\" title=\"Little My has started 15 conversations\">\n\t\t    <img src=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/avatars/21678/avatar-bpfull-bpthumb.jpg\" class=\"avatar user-21678-avatar avatar-96 photo\" width=\"96\" height=\"96\" alt=\"Profile photo of Little My\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role member-avatar-badge\">Member</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a class=\"url fn n\" href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/littlemy/profile/\" title=\"Little My has started 15 conversations\" rel=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\tLittle My\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-20T10:14:31+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 20, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline -->\n\t<div class=\"entry-sub-actions\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/#comments\" title=\"40 Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">40</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p>Sometime in the spring of 1976, the rabbi found out that Mindy’s husband was smoking with his Sunday School students. They were the usual rum lot of high school age boys whose interest in religion had ceased with the cashing of their Bar Mitzvah checks; they put up with Eliyahu’s class for the sake of a reliable source of weed. A very unpleasant conference with the rabbi and the synagogue board was followed by a heated exchange with several outraged parents. Mindy and Eliyahu decided it was time to fulfill their dream of “making aliyah” — moving permanently to Israel. As their departure date neared, Mindy asked if I wanted to take over her job as <em>balanit</em> or attendant, at the mikveh.\n</p><p>The San Francisco mikveh (“ritual bath”) was in the Bnai David synagogue in the Mission District. Built in 1908 after the Earthquake, most of the congregation by then had long since departed, but the mikveh remained in use. Orthodox synagogues do not necessarily include a mikveh in their building plans, but this congregation, established in the 1880s by Eastern European Jews, was the first strictly Orthodox community in San Francisco. It is said that people came from as far away as Nevada to use the mikveh. The pool was unusually large — a dozen people could immerse at one time.</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/\" class=\"more-link fr button\">More</a>  <div class=\"ricochet-share-toolbar\">\n    <a title=\"Share this Post on Facebook.\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/\" target=\"_blank\">\n      <img alt=\"Share on Facebook.\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/themes/boss-child/images/ricoshare/facebook.png\" class=\"fa fa-facebook\">\n    </a>\n    <a title=\"Share this Post on Twitter.\" href=\"https://twitter.com/share?url=https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/&amp;text=+%40ricochet\" target=\"_blank\">\n      <img alt=\"Share on Twitter.\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/themes/boss-child/images/ricoshare/twitter.png\" class=\"fa fa-twitter\">\n    </a>\n    <a href=\"mailto:?subject=From+Ricochet.com&amp;body=https://ricochet.com/423774/balanit-my-life-as-a-mikveh-lady/\" target=\"_blank\">\n      <img alt=\"Share by email.\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/themes/boss-child/images/ricoshare/email.png\" title=\"Email this Post to a friend.\" class=\"fa fa-envelope\">\n    </a>\n      </div>\n  \t\t</div><!-- class=\"clear\">\n  \t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">\n              \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423970/georgias-6th-whats-it-mean-for-trump-and-gop/\" title=\"Permalink to Georgia’s 6th: What Does It Mean for Trump and the GOP?\" rel=\"bookmark\">Georgia’s 6th: What Does It Mean for Trump and the GOP?</a>\n                      </h1>\n          <div class=\"entry-meta table\">\n            <div class=\"table-cell\">\n              \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar coolidge-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a Kirker\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role coolidge-avatar-badge\">Coolidge</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a              <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <h3>The short answer: nothing!</h3>\n<figure class=\"figure wp-caption alignnone\"><img class=\"wp-image-423983 size-large\" src=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-600x259.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"259\" srcset=\"https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-600x259.jpg 600w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-150x65.jpg 150w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-300x130.jpg 300w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-768x332.jpg 768w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-624x270.jpg 624w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff-750x324.jpg 750w, https://cdn.ricochet.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ossoff.jpg 828w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Graphic: The New York Times.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As you probably know, Georgia’s 6th Congressional District was previously held by Tom Price, who is now the Secretary of Health and Human Services, which is why the seat was subject to a jungle primary between Democrat Jon Ossoff and 11 Republicans.\n</p><p>Price won the district by double digits in November while Trump barely defeated Clinton. The seat has been held by a Republican since the Carter presidency, so how unusual is it that Jon Ossoff won 48% of the vote?</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a format-standard hentry category-culture tag-andrea-del-castagno tag-easter tag-florence tag-gospel-of-john tag-last-supper tag-perspective tag-renaissance odd\">\n\t<!-- Search, Blog index, archives, single blog post -->\n\t\t\t<div class=\"boxed-content\">\n\t\t\t<header class=\"clear\">\n  \t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">\n              \t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423862/andrea-del-castagno-last-supper/\" title=\"Permalink to Andrea del Castagno, Last Supper\" rel=\"bookmark\">Andrea del Castagno, <em>Last Supper</em></a>\n                      </h1>\n          <div class=\"entry-meta table\">\n            <div class=\"table-cell\">\n              \t<div class=\"entry-meta\">\n\t\t<div class=\"entry-avatar contributor-avatar-badge with-badge\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/titustechera/profile/\" title=\"Titus Techera has started 249 conversations\">\n\t\t    <img src=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/avatars/26903/5784ffb097c66-bpfull.jpg\" class=\"avatar user-26903-avatar avatar-96 photo\" width=\"96\" height=\"96\" alt=\"Profile photo of Titus Techera\">\t\t\t\t<span class=\"author-role contributor-avatar-badge\">Contributor</span>\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author-byline\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a class=\"url fn n\" href=\"https://ricochet.com/members/titustechera/profile/\" title=\"Titus Techera has started 249 conversations\" rel=\"author\">\n\t\t\t\t\tTitus Techera\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<time class=\"entry-date published\" datetime=\"2017-04-19T13:30:09+00:00\">\n\n\tApril 19, 2017\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t</div><!-- .author-byline -->\n\t<div class=\"entry-sub-actions\">\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423862/andrea-del-castagno-last-supper/#comments\" title=\"22 Comments\">\n<span class=\"entry-comments\">22</span>\n\t\tCOMMENTS\n\t</a></div>\t</div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n      <div class=\"divider\">&nbsp;</div>\n                      <div style=\"padding-left:0;padding-right:0;\" class=\"entry-content entry-summary \">\n      <p><a href=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo.jpg\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-344087 size-large\" src=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-970x474.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"293\" srcset=\"https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-970x474.jpg 970w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-960x469.jpg 960w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-500x244.jpg 500w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-768x375.jpg 768w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-60x29.jpg 60w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-192x94.jpg 192w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo-800x391.jpg 800w, https://7373-presscdn-0-43-pagely.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/del-castagno-andrea-cenacolo.jpg 1400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a>\n</p><p>This very large fresco has been a secret for most of its history. It was painted in the 1440s for the cloistered nuns of Santa Apollonia in Florence, which is why it was very rarely seen by outsiders. Eventually, it was covered in plaster, which is why it’s so well preserved, unlike the scenes above it. We have it rediscovered only since the suppression of the nuns by the military in the 1860s, and can now marvel at the poetic effect it achieves and see in what its greatness consists. Indeed, authorship itself was unwittingly a secret, but that, too, has been resolved. The last secret, not likely of resolution, is the story of the author. Castagno is little known except by slander and by his works, and the slander is not honest either. The most famous chronicler of Renaissance Italy, Vasari, offers a great big lie of a story accusing him of murdering another painter out of jealousy–so far as anyone can tell, the lie is meant to explain the dramatic quality of Castagno’s painting–his characters have no softness about them. Art history could step in to help us in our time of need, explaining what painting looked like before him and afterward, but that’s too much of a distraction. We can only attend to the mysteries in the painting itself.</p> <div class=\"clear\"></div>\n<a href=\"https://ricochet.com/423862/andrea-del-castagno-last-supper/\" class=\"more-link fr button\">More</a>  <div class=\"ricochet-share-toolbar\">\n    <a title=\"Share this Post on Facebook.\"
